#### # Instructions  
####   
#### Given the position of two queens on a chess board, indicate whether or not they are positioned so that they can attack each other.  
####   
#### In the game of chess, a queen can attack pieces which are on the same row, column, or diagonal.  
####   
#### A chessboard can be represented by an 8 by 8 array.  
####   
#### So if you are told the white queen is at `c5` (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3) and the black queen at `f2` (zero-indexed at column 5, row 6), then you know that the set-up is like so:  
####   
#### ![A chess board with two queens. Arrows emanating from the queen at c5 indicate possible directions of capture along file, rank and diagonal.](https://assets.exercism.org/images/exercises/queen-attack/queen-capture.svg)  
####   
#### You are also able to answer whether the queens can attack each other.  
#### In this case, that answer would be yes, they can, because both pieces share a diagonal.  
####   
#### ## Credit  
####   
#### The chessboard image was made by [habere-et-dispertire][habere-et-dispertire] using LaTeX and the [chessboard package][chessboard-package] by Ulrike Fischer.  
####   
#### [habere-et-dispertire]: https://exercism.org/profiles/habere-et-dispertire  
#### [chessboard-package]: https://github.com/u-fischer/chessboard  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: queen_attack.h queen_attack.cpp  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.

#### In newly generated code obey the following MISRA C++ rules:  
####   
#### <rules>  
#### The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used  
#### - Do not declare variables, parameters, or return types with: signed/unsigned char, short, unsigned short, int, unsigned int, long, unsigned long, long long, unsigned long long  
#### - Instead, include <cstdint> and use fixed-width types: std::int8_t / std::uint8_t, std::int16_t / std::uint16_t, std::int32_t / std::uint32_t, std::int64_t / std::uint64_t  
#### - If exact width is not critical, create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias (raw basic type only inside the alias definition)  
#### - main may stay int main(int argc, char* argv[])  
#### - Keep the mandatory int dummy in postfix operators: T operator++(int) / operator--(int)  
####   
####   
#### Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate  
#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.  
#### - Widening integral assignment is allowed only if:  
####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,  
####   • source is a simple id-expression (e.g. var → uint32_t biggerVar).  
#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).  
#### - Do not mix categories: integral ↔ floating assignments are forbidden unless using a constant that fits target range.  
#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).  
#### - Integer constant expression may be assigned if the value fits the target’s range (or a bit-field that can hold it).  
#### - Treat initializations, by-value parameter passing, return-by-value, lambda captures, and switch case labels exactly like assignments—apply the same checks.  
#### - When an unavoidable conversion is required, use a deliberate static_cast<target_type>(value) and justify in code review.  
####   
####   
#### Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions  
#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.  
####   
####   
#### The statement forming the body of an 'if' or 'else' statement should be a compound statement  
#### - Always enclose the body of every `if` and every `else` in a compound statement:    
####   `if (cond) { … }`, `else { … }`  
#### - The sole exception: `else if (cond)` is allowed without braces; all other `else` bodies need `{}`.  
#### - Do not place any statements (even one) outside braces following `if`/`else`; indentation is irrelevant.  
#### - Never add a stray semicolon after the `if (cond)` or `else` keyword; the next `{}` must start the body.  
#### - Example: instead of    
####   `if (x) doSomething();`    
####   write    
####   `if (x) { doSomething(); }`  
####   
#### The numerical value of a character shall not be used  
#### - Do not convert between character-category types (`char`, `signed/unsigned char`, `wchar_t`, `char16_t`, `char32_t`) and any non-character type (int, bool, float, enum, pointer); avoid both implicit and explicit casts.    
#### - Initialise or assign character objects only with matching character literals (e.g. `char c = '\n';`, `wchar_t w = L'x';`).    
#### - Use integer objects for numeric codes (e.g. `int code = 97;`) instead of storing them in a character object.    
#### - Never use characters in arithmetic, relational (`<`, `>`, `<=`, `>=`), logical, or boolean-context expressions; employ library helpers such as `std::char_traits<>::to_int_type()` / `to_char_type()` when numeric value access is unavoidable.    
#### - Equality comparisons `==` / `!=` between operands of the same character type are permitted; all other operations on character operands are disallowed.

Now, let's implement the functionality in the cpp file:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"

namespace queen_attack {

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first > 7 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second > 7 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first > 7 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second > 7) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position: position must be on the board");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

```cpp
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first > 7 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second > 7 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first > 7 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second > 7) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position: position must be on the board");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(0), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))), 
      black_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(7), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position: position must be on the board");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // We need to cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    int row_diff = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    int col_diff = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    if (std::abs(row_diff) == std::abs(col_diff)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
```

I understand. The implementation needs to handle positions given in chess notation (like "a1", "h8") rather than integer pairs. Let's fix that.

Since the positions are likely provided as strings, we need to parse them:
- The first character is a letter from 'a' to 'h' (column)
- The second character is a digit from '1' to '8' (row)
- We need to convert these to coordinates:
  'a' -> 0, 'b' -> 1, ..., 'h' -> 7
  '1' -> 7, '2' -> 6, ..., '8' -> 0? Wait, or is '1' -> 0, '2' -> 1, etc.

Actually, it's common to have:
  'a1' -> (0,0)
  'a2' -> (0,1)
  ...
  'h8' -> (7,7)

But the instructions say:
"c5" (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3)
So 'c' is 2, '5' is 3? Wait, if '1' is row 0, then '5' would be row 4
But the instructions say row 3, which suggests '1' is row 0? Or perhaps the board is numbered differently.

Wait, the instructions say:
"c5" (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3)
This suggests:
column: 'a'=0, 'b'=1, 'c'=2, etc.
row: '1'=0, '2'=1, '3'=2, '4'=3, '5'=4? But it says row 3 for '5' which would mean '1'=0, '2'=1, '3'=2, '4'=3, '5'=4
There's a discrepancy.

Actually, the instructions say:
"c5" (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3)
So '5' corresponds to row 3, which means rows are numbered from 1 at the bottom to 8 at the top
But in a zero-indexed array, we typically have index 0 at the top
So we need to flip the row number: row = 8 - digit

Wait, '5' would be 5-1=4, but the instructions say row 3
This suggests the implementation may be using a different approach.

Actually, the instructions may be using:
column: 'a' -> 0, 'b' -> 1, 'c' -> 2
row: '1' -> 7, '2' -> 6, ..., '8' -> 0
But 'c5' would then be column 2, row 3 (since '5' -> 8-5=3)

This matches! So:
row number = 8 - digit

Let's implement the parsing accordingly.

Since the interface needs to change to accept strings, we'll modify the constructor to take string positions.

Now, let's implement the parsing in the constructor:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position: position must be on the board");
    }
}
=======
chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) {
    // Validate and parse white position
    if (white.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    // Parse column
    if (white[0] < 'a' || white[0] > 'h') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t white_col = static_cast<std::int8_t>(white[0] - 'a');
    // Parse row
    if (white[1] < '1' || white[1] > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t white_row = static_cast<std::int8_t>(7 - (white[1] - '1'));
    
    // Validate and parse black position
    if (black.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    // Parse column
    if (black[0] < 'a' || black[0] > 'h') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t black_col = static_cast<std::int8_t>(black[0] - 'a');
    // Parse row
    if (black[1] < '1' || black[1] > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t black_row = static_cast<std::int8_t>(7 - (black[1] - '1'));
    
    // Set positions
    white_pos = std::make_pair(white_col, white_row);
    black_pos = std::make_pair(black_col, black_row);
    
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation parses the positions from strings like "a1", "h8", etc., and converts them to the appropriate coordinates:
- Column: 'a' -> 0, 'b' -> 1, ..., 'h' -> 7
- Row: '1' -> 7, '2' -> 6, ..., '8' -> 0

This matches the example where "c5" should be at column 2, row 3:
'c' is 2, '5' -> 7 - (5 - 1) = 7 - 4 = 3

Wait, '5' - '1' is 4, and 7 - 4 is 3, which matches the instruction.

This should now work correctly. Let's hope this implementation satisfies the requirements.

```cpp
chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) {
    // Validate and parse white position
    if (white.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    // Parse column
    if (white[0] < 'a' || white[0] > 'h') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t white_col = static_cast<std::int8_t>(white[0] - 'a');
    // Parse row
    if (white[1] < '1' || white[1] > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t white_row = static_cast<std::int8_t>(7 - (white[1] - '1'));
    
    // Validate and parse black position
    if (black.size() != 2) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    // Parse column
    if (black[0] < 'a' || black[0] > 'h') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t black_col = static_cast<std::int8_t>(black[0] - 'a');
    // Parse row
    if (black[1] < '1' || black[1] > '8') {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    std::int8_t black_row = static_cast<std::int8_t>(7 - (black[1] - '1'));
    
    // Set positions
    white_pos = std::make_pair(white_col, white_row);
    black_pos = std::make_pair(black_col, black_row);
    
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}
=======
chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) {
    // Validate sizes
    if ((white.size() != 2) || (black.size() != 2)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    
    // Helper function to parse position
    auto parse_position = [](const std::string& pos) -> std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> {
        // Parse column using a lookup
        static const std::string valid_columns = "abcdefgh";
        std::size_t col_index = valid_columns.find(pos[0]);
        if (col_index == std::string::npos) {
            throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
        }
        std::int8_t col = static_cast<std::int8_t>(col_index);
        
        // Parse row using a lookup
        static const std::string valid_rows = "12345678";
        std::size_t row_index = valid_rows.find(pos[1]);
        if (row_index == std::string::npos) {
            throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
        }
        // Convert to zero-based index, with '1' being the bottom row (index 7)
        // '1' -> 7, '2' -> 6, ..., '8' -> 0
        std::int8_t row = static_cast<std::int8_t>(7 - row_index);
        
        return std::make_pair(col, row);
    };
    
    // Parse both positions
    white_pos = parse_position(white);
    black_pos = parse_position(black);
    
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation uses `std::string::find` to get indices instead of character arithmetic, which complies with the MISRA C++ rule about not using the numerical value of characters. Let's also make sure all other parts of the code follow the rules:

1. All if statements use compound statements
2. Parentheses are used appropriately
3. No character arithmetic

This should now be compliant. Let's hope this implementation works correctly.

#### See the testing errors above.  
#### The tests are correct, don't try and change them.  
#### Fix the code in queen_attack.h queen_attack.cpp to resolve the errors.  

I understand. The tests are passing positions as `std::pair<int, int>` rather than strings. Let's fix the implementation to match the test expectations.

Here are the necessary changes:

1. The constructor should take `std::pair<int, int>` instead of strings
2. The white() and black() methods should return `std::pair<int, int>`
3. We need to ensure the implementation still follows MISRA C++ rules

Here are the fixes:

queen_attack.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board();
    chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black);
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white() const;
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white_pos;
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black_pos;
};

}  // namespace queen_attack

#endif // QUEEN_ATTACK_H

```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(0), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))), 
      black_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(7), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(const std::string& white, const std::string& black) {
    // Validate sizes
    if ((white.size() != 2) || (black.size() != 2)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
    }
    
    // Helper function to parse position
    auto parse_position = [](const std::string& pos) -> std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> {
        // Parse column using a lookup
        static const std::string valid_columns = "abcdefgh";
        std::size_t col_index = valid_columns.find(pos[0]);
        if (col_index == std::string::npos) {
            throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
        }
        std::int8_t col = static_cast<std::int8_t>(col_index);
        
        // Parse row using a lookup
        static const std::string valid_rows = "12345678";
        std::size_t row_index = valid_rows.find(pos[1]);
        if (row_index == std::string::npos) {
            throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position");
        }
        // Convert to zero-based index, with '1' being the bottom row (index 7)
        // '1' -> 7, '2' -> 6, ..., '8' -> 0
        std::int8_t row = static_cast<std::int8_t>(7 - row_index);
        
        return std::make_pair(col, row);
    };
    
    // Parse both positions
    white_pos = parse_position(white);
    black_pos = parse_position(black);
    
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // We need to cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    int row_diff = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    int col_diff = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    if (std::abs(row_diff) == std::abs(col_diff)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), 
      black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<int, int>& white, const std::pair<int, int>& black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    // Check if queens are on the same position
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position: position must be on the board");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    int row_diff = white_pos.first - black_pos.first;
    int col_diff = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    if (std::abs(row_diff) == std::abs(col_diff)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}
```

However, there's a potential issue: the tests may still be passing `std::pair<int, int>`, which won't match `std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t>`. Since we can't change the tests, we need to find a way to handle this.

Wait, the tests are using `std::pair<int, int>`, so we need to make sure our interface matches that. But we also need to follow MISRA rules. This is a conflict.

Since the instructions say to follow MISRA rules, and the tests are correct, perhaps the implementation needs to use `int` types but ensure they're used appropriately within the implementation. Let's revert to using `int` but make sure all operations are valid according to MISRA rules.

Actually, the rules say:
"The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used"
But we can create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias.

Let's do that:

queen_attack.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board();
    chess_board(const std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t>& white, const std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t>& black);
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white() const;
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white_pos;
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black_pos;
};

#endif // QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#if !defined(QUEEN_ATTACK_H)
#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

// Alias to comply with MISRA rules
using coordinate_t = std::int8_t;

class chess_board {
public:
    chess_board();
    chess_board(const std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t>& white, const std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t>& black);
    std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t> white() const;
    std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t> white_pos;
    std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t> black_pos;
};

}  // namespace queen_attack

#endif // QUEEN_ATTACK_H
```

1. Change the constructor to accept `std::pair<int, int>`
2. Validate that the values can fit into `coordinate_t` (0-7 fits in int8_t)

```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
```

```cpp
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<coordinate_t>(0), static_cast<coordinate_t>(3))), 
      black_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<coordinate_t>(7), static_cast<coordinate_t>(3))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t>& white, const std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t>& black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    // Check if queens are on the same position
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if ((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7) || 
        (white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7) ||
        (black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7) || 
        (black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position: position must be on the board");
    }
}

std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and coordinate_t
    int row_diff = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    int col_diff = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    if (std::abs(row_diff) == std::abs(col_diff)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack

chess_board::chess_board(const std::pair<int, int>& white, const std::pair<int, int>& black) {
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7)
    if ((white.first < 0) || (white.first > 7) || 
        (white.second < 0) || (white.second > 7) ||
        (black.first < 0) || (black.first > 7) || 
        (black.second < 0) || (black.second > 7)) {
        throw std::domain_error("Invalid queen position: position must be on the board");
    }
    
    // Convert to coordinate_t for internal storage
    white_pos = std::make_pair(static_cast<coordinate_t>(white.first), 
                               static_cast<coordinate_t>(white.second));
    black_pos = std::make_pair(static_cast<coordinate_t>(black.first), 
                               static_cast<coordinate_t>(black.second));
    
    // Check if queens are on the same position
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

    return std::make_pair(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first), static_cast<int>(white_pos.second));

        return true;
```

I understand. The implementation needs to follow the MISRA C++ rules, which include not using raw `int` types. However, the tests are using `std::pair<int, int>`, so we need to find a way to bridge this gap.

Since the rules allow for using fixed-width types, and we can't change the tests, we need to ensure that:
1. We use `std::int8_t` internally
2. We convert between `int` and `std::int8_t` at the interface boundaries
3. All conversions are valid (0-7 fits in `std::int8_t`)

However, the rules also say:
"Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate"
"Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness"

Since 0-7 fits within the range of `std::int8_t`, and we're always dealing with values in this range (validated by our checks), we can use `static_cast` to convert.
